Runner-up is TICT because the molecule has multiple torsion axes that could twist in S1, but the absence of clear donor/acceptor groups makes strong CT/TICT character uncertain. Top1 remains a working hypothesis because many neutral polyaryls can still show excited-state twisting, excimer/aggregate emission, or subtle CT-like states depending on conformation and packing; distinguishing neutral-aromatic RIM vs TICT needs excited-state electronic character (e.g., oscillator strength changes, charge redistribution) and torsion dependence. Shared prepared structure context is available (prepared XYZ/SDF, conformer set). Macro can provide a literature/structure-heuristic mechanism assessment (RIM vs CT/TICT vs ESIPT) but cannot prove excited-state character. Microscopic can run bounded, low-cost computations (aTB S0 optimization and limited S1 vertical excitations) to check whether low-energy excitations look locally excited vs CT-like and whether twisting is energetically favored, but cannot do exhaustive packing/crystal simulations in the first round. Therefore the first round should gather both macro (mechanistic priors from structure class) and microscopic (quick electronic-structure indicators) evidence.

### Round 1 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (strengthened). Top2=TICT (slightly weakened but still plausible). Latest evidence: macro topology (neutral all-hydrocarbon; aromatic rings=6; donor_acceptor_partition_proxy=0.0) supports neutral aromatic and disfavors ICT/ESIPT. Microscopic baseline shows a bright lowest excited state (S1 energy=3.944 eV, oscillator strength=0.307; lowest_state_is_bright) and very small S0 dipole (~0.065 D), which is more typical of locally excited neutral aromatic transitions than CT-dominated states; however, torsional flexibility remains (5 rotors), so a TICT-like relaxation could still emerge beyond vertical excitations. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs TICT): whether twisting along key aryl–vinyl/aryl–aryl dihedrals produces a lower-energy emissive state with reduced oscillator strength and increased charge separation (CT descriptors) relative to the vertical bright state. Verifier supplementation is missing; closure justification is missing. Best next action now is a targeted microscopic low-cost torsion-snapshot scan with CT-descriptor extraction to directly test torsion-induced CT/brightness loss that would support TICT over neutral aromatic.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.72

- task_instruction: Run a bounded torsion-snapshot sensitivity task to discriminate neutral aromatic vs TICT: (1) select the most relevant aryl–exocyclic and/or aryl–aryl dihedral(s) among the 5 torsion candidates adjacent to the central C=C/triarylmethine-like core; (2) generate ~8 snapshots over 0–90° (or -90–90°) for 1–2 key dihedrals; (3) for each snapshot, compute vertical S1/S2 energies and oscillator strengths (at same low-cost level as baseline); (4) extract/estimate CT descriptors from the existing baseline_bundle and from torsion snapshots (e.g., charge separation, dipole change proxy, electron-hole separation proxy if available) using extract_ct_descriptors_from_bundle / parse_snapshot_outputs; (5) report whether twisting yields (a) a stabilized low-oscillator-strength state and (b) increased CT character, which would support TICT, vs relatively torsion-insensitive bright LE behavior, which would support neutral aromatic. If job submission fails, report the registry error and return no artifact_bundle_id.

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (0.74) vs Top2=TICT (0.16). ### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (0.66) vs Top2=TICT (0.24). Latest evidence partially challenges the top1: the new bounded torsion snapshots (dihedral dih_6_7_8_9 at 30/60/90°) show that increasing twist can reduce oscillator strength and yield a pattern where the lowest state is dark and a higher state is brighter, which is a classic qualitative hallmark expected under TICT-like state reordering (though it can also arise from symmetry/selection-rule effects without strong CT). This strengthens the TICT challenger relative to prior rounds where torsion evidence was missing. However, verifier evidence still supports neutral aromatic as the default for all-hydrocarbon polyaryl alkenes unless special symmetry-breaking CT conditions apply, and we still lack molecule-specific CT descriptors (electron–hole separation, excited-state dipole change) to confirm the dark state is CT-like. Key remaining discriminator: whether the torsion-stabilized dark S1 exhibits increased charge separation / large excited-state dipole (TICT) versus remaining locally excited but symmetry-forbidden (neutral aromatic). Verifier supplementation status is sufficient; closure justification is still collecting (internal) because we now have torsion-driven brightness changes but not CT-metric confirmation. Next action should therefore be a single atomic microscopic step that extracts CT descriptors from the new torsion snapshot bundle (and baseline bundle for comparison) to directly test TICT vs neutral aromatic.

### Round 7 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (0.62) vs Top2=TICT (0.29). Latest evidence partially challenges Top1: torsion snapshots produce a dark lowest excited state at high twist (lowest_state_is_dark_then_bright; very low f at ~90°), which is compatible with TICT-like behavior. However, the attempted CT-descriptor extraction found that the key CT metrics (excited-state dipole, CT distance, transition charge difference, localization proxy) are unavailable in the snapshot artifacts, so the critical discriminator (whether the dark torsion-stabilized state is truly CT in character) remains unresolved. Verifier supplementation remains sufficient and continues to support Top1 in general (TICT in all-hydrocarbon systems is atypical and usually requires symmetry breaking/environmental coupling), but internal closure justification is still collecting because molecule-specific CT confirmation is missing. Best next action is a bounded microscopic step to extract CT descriptors from the baseline bundle (round_01_baseline_bundle) to at least establish whether any CT proxies are available there (and/or to confirm they are also unavailable), enabling either (a) a decisive comparison if baseline has CT metrics, or (b) a best-available closure justification if CT metrics are unavailable across both baseline and torsion snapshots.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.62
